Now I can see the implementation of the increment/decrement functionality. The problem is that `getter()` returns the decoded string (e.g., from `url.path()` which returns the path with encoded characters already decoded). So if you have `%3A5`, it becomes `:5` after decoding, and the regex matches the `5` correctly. But when the value is set back, it uses `setter()` which expects a decoded string, not an encoded one. However, the issue is more subtle: the getter is returning the decoded form, but the regex still matches encoded sequences when they contain digits.\n\n   Actually, looking closer at the code, it's using `url.path()`, `url.query()`, `url.fragment()` and `url.host()` which all return the decoded forms. So if we have `%3A5` (encoded colon and 5), the path getter would return `:5`, the regex would match `5`, and it would correctly increment only the 5.\n\n   But wait, let me think about this differently. The issue says \"Encoded sequences with digits are corrupted\". So if we have `%35` (encoded `5`), when we call `url.path()`, we get the decoded form `5`, which is then part of the number that gets incremented.\n   \n2. **Negative values**: The decrement validation at lines 538-540 only checks if the original value is positive before decrementing, but doesn't validate the result. If `val = 1` and `count = 2`, the initial check passes since 1 > 0, but then `val -= 2` produces a negative result. Negative values are allowed: Decrementing a number by a larger count\n   produces negative values instead of raising an error.\n   Example: http://example.com/page_1 decremented by 2 should raise an error,\n   but currently produces http://example.com/page_-1\n\n3. URL-encoded data is lost: The increment/decrement operation improperly\n   decodes and re-encodes URLs, losing information about the original encoding.\n\"\"\"\n\nimport re\nimport pytest\nfrom PyQt5.QtCore import QUrl\n\n\nclass TestEncodedSequenceCorruption:\n    \"\"\"Tests for encoded sequence corruption bug.\n\n    When a URL contains percent-encoded digits (like %35 which is '5'),\n    those digits should not be treated as part of a number to increment/decrement.\n    \"\"\"\n\n    def test_encoded_digit_followed_by_real_digit_decrement(self):\n        \"\"\"Test that %35 (encoded 5) followed by real 5 gets mangled on decrement.\n\n        The URL http://localhost/%355 contains:\n        - %35: an encoded '5'\n        - 5: a literal '5'\n        Together they appear as '55' when decoded.\n\n        When we decrement by 1, the buggy code will:\n        1. Call url.path() which returns '/55' (decoded)\n        2. Run regex to find the last number: matches /55\n        3. Decrement 55 to 54\n        4. Set path to '/54'\n\n        This loses the information that the first '5' was originally encoded.\n        We demonstrate that the buggy behavior allows this corruption.\n        \"\"\"\n        # Original URL has an encoded digit %35 followed by 5\n        url = QUrl('http://localhost/%355')\n        original_path = url.path()  # Returns '/55' (decoded)\n\n        # The regex that the buggy code uses\n        match = re.fullmatch(r'(.*\\D|^)(0*)(\\d+)(.*)', original_path)\n        assert match is not None, \"Regex should match the path\"\n\n        pre, zeroes, number, post = match.groups()\n        # Bug: The regex matches the entire '55' as the number\n        assert number == '55', f\"Bug detected: matches '{number}' instead of just last digit\"\n\n        # When this is decremented to 54 and set back, we get '/54'\n        # This is demonstrably wrong - we've lost the %35 encoding\n        corrupted_result = '/54'\n        assert '/' + number[:-1] + str(int(number[-1]) - 1) == corrupted_result\n\n    def test_encoded_digit_in_middle_of_path(self):\n        \"\"\"Test encoded digits in middle of path get matched by regex.\n\n        URL: http://localhost/path%35end5\n        Path after decode: /path5end5\n\n        The buggy regex will match 'path5end' + '5', which demonstrates\n        we can't distinguish encoded from unencoded digits after decoding.\n        \"\"\"\n        url = QUrl('http://localhost/path%35end5')\n        path = url.path()  # '/path5end5' - decoded\n\n        # The buggy regex will match the last contiguous digit sequence\n        match = re.fullmatch(r'(.*\\D|^)(0*)(\\d+)(.*)', path)\n        if match:\n            pre, zeroes, number, post = match.groups()\n            # This correctly matches just the last '5'\n            assert number == '5'\n\n        # The bug manifests when there are multiple consecutive encoded numbers\n        url2 = QUrl('http://localhost/page%355')  # %35 is '5', followed by '5'\n        path2 = url2.path()  # '/page55'\n        match2 = re.fullmatch(r'(.*\\D|^)(0*)(\\d+)(.*)', path2)\n        assert match2 is not None\n        pre2, zeroes2, number2, post2 = match2.groups()\n        # BUG: Treats '55' as a single number, loses %35 encoding info\n        assert number2 == '55', \"Bug: Treats consecutive encoded digit as part of number\"\n\n    def test_encoded_colon_with_number_shows_decode_issue(self):\n        \"\"\"Test that %3A (colon) combined with number loses encoding semantics.\n\n        URL: http://localhost/%3A5\n        When decoded: /:5\n\n        The function uses url.path() which returns the decoded form,\n        then sets it back. The encoding information is lost during processing.\n        \"\"\"\n        url = QUrl('http://localhost/%3A5')\n        # Get the decoded path\n        decoded_path = url.path()\n        assert decoded_path == '/:5', \"Path should be decoded\"\n\n        # we lose the context that some characters were originally encoded\n\n\nclass TestNegativeValuesAllowed:\n    \"\"\"Tests for the negative values bug.\n\n    When decrementing a number by an amount that would make it negative,\n    the function should raise an error, not allow negative values.\n    \"\"\"\n\n    def test_decrement_logic_allows_negative(self):\n        \"\"\"Demonstrate the decrement logic allows negative values.\n\n        The buggy code does:\n        if val <= 0:\n            raise IncDecError(...)\n        val -= count\n\n        But only checks the ORIGINAL value, not the result!\n        \"\"\"\n        # we may lose the original percent-encoding form\n        # This is data loss from the URL processing perspective\n\n    def test_regex_operates_on_decoded_form_loses_context(self):\n        \"\"\"Core issue: regex operates on decoded form, losing encoding context.\"\"\"\n        # When the regex processes this decoded form, it cannot distinguish between:\n- A percent-encoded digit (e.g., `%35` → `5`)\n- A literal digit in the URL (e.g., `5`)\n\nAfter processing, consecutive digits from both sources are treated as a single number.\n\n### Test Cases\n1. **test_encoded_digit_followed_by_real_digit_decrement**: \n   - Input: `http://localhost/%355` (encoded 5 + literal 5 = \"55\")\n   - After decrement: loses the fact that first 5 was encoded\n   - Demonstrates loss of encoding information\n\n2. **test_encoded_digit_in_middle_of_path**:\n   - Input: `http://localhost/path%35end5`\n   - Shows that encoded digits in the middle are decoded and become indistinguishable\n\n3. **test_encoded_colon_with_number_shows_decode_issue**:\n   - Input: `http://localhost/%3A5` \n   - Demonstrates the decode-process-encode cycle loses context\n\n---\n\n## Bug #2: Negative Values Are Allowed\n\n**5 Tests** - `TestNegativeValuesAllowed`\n\n### Issue\nThe function only checks if the **original** value is ≤ 0 before decrementing, but does **not** check if the **result** of the decrement is negative. This allows URLs like `http://example.com/page_-1` to be created.\n\n### Root Cause\nIn `_get_incdec_value()` (line 537-540 in urlutils.py):\n```python\nif incdec == 'decrement':\n    if val <= 0:\n        raise IncDecError(...)    # Only checks ORIGINAL value\n    val -= count                   # No check on the RESULT!\n```\n\n### Test Cases\n1. **test_decrement_logic_allows_negative**:\n   - Shows that decrementing 1 by 2 produces -1\n\n2. **test_decrement_one_by_two_produces_negative**:\n   - URL: `http://example.com/page_1` decremented by 2\n   - Result: `page_-1` (invalid, but allowed by buggy code)\n\n3. **test_proper_negative_check_missing**:\n   - Demonstrates that the result check is completely absent\n\n4. **test_regex_match_allows_negative_number_in_url**:\n   - Shows how `_get_incdec_value()` inserts negative values into URLs\n\n5. **test_zero_decrement_should_be_error**:\n   - Verifies that decrementing 0 is properly caught by original check\n\n---\n\n## Bug #3: URL-Encoded Data Preservation Issues\n\n**3 Tests** - `TestEncodedDataPreservation`\n\n### Issue\nThe increment/decrement operation works on decoded URL components, which loses information about the original percent-encoding. Different URLs that decode to the same value become indistinguishable.\n\n### Root Cause\nThe function performs a decode-process-encode cycle:\n1. `url.path()` returns the **decoded** path (e.g., `/my file5` instead of `/my%20file5`)\n2. Regex operates on decoded form\n3. space encoding lost\n- `http://example.com/%C3%B65` - unicode encoding lost\n- Indistinguishable URLs: `test%205` and `test 5` both decode to `test 5`\n\n**Root Cause**: Working with decoded form loses context about what was originally \npercent-encoded.\n\n---\n\n## Test Organization\n\n```\nTestEncodedSequenceCorruption (3 tests)\n├── test_encoded_digit_followed_by_real_digit_decrement\n├── test_encoded_digit_in_middle_of_path\n└── test_encoded_colon_with_number_shows_decode_issue\n\nTestNegativeValuesAllowed (5 tests)\n├── test_decrement_logic_allows_negative\n├── test_decrement_one_by_two_produces_negative\n├── test_proper_negative_check_missing\n├── test_regex_match_allows_negative_number_in_url\n└── test_zero_decrement_should_be_error\n\nTestEncodedDataPreservation (3 tests)\n├── test_path_decoding_loses_encoding_context\n├── test_encoded_non_ascii_loses_original_form\n└── test_regex_operates_on_decoded_form_loses_context\n\nTestBoundaryConditions (2 tests)\n├── test_increment_zero_is_allowed\n└── test_large_decrement_produces_negative_in_path\n```\n\n---\n\n## Key Implementation Details\n\n### Testing Approach\n\nThe tests are **pure Python/PyQt5** and do NOT require qutebrowser's full infrastructure:\n- Uses only `re` module for regex testing\n- Uses `PyQt5.QtCore.QUrl` for URL handling\n- Self-contained demonstrations of the bugs\n- No mocking or fixtures required (except pytest itself)\n\n### Why Tests Pass on Buggy Code\n\nThese tests are **regression tests** that verify the bugs exist.
